1. Welcome to the ZB group!
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 04:06:25 -0000

Hello and welcome to the ZB group! This group is dedicated to discussion of the Zborowski-Bruchem speedsolving method. This group is open to learners, skeptics, or anyone who just wants to find out what the ZB method is about. I am personally learning ZB and feel that it has potential to be a fast method. Feel free to post anything about ZB on this group. Chris

7. How I learn ZB and can this be improved on?
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 05:21:43 -0000

Hey everyone, I hope this group continues to grow as I would really like to see this method become mainstream one day in the future, assuming is has the potential of course. Here is how I have learned what I know of ZB so far. It has worked for me, but I don't know if it is the best way. I would like this thread to be a discussion of the most efficient way to learn ZB. I guess this of course assumes you already know all of OLL and PLL. Or at the very very least all of PLL. Very first beginnings: I guess at the very start I learned the COLL algs before anything else. COLL recognition is such a core part of ZBLL recognition, that I think it is very important to learn these very early on. Moving on: After COLL I moved on to ZBF2L algs. I was basing off Macky's quote that "It's all about F2L" and I think for ZB it will most definitely be true that "It's all about ZBF2L" in terms of whether a solve is a good solve or not. I've known the ZBF2L algs now for 8 months and I am starting to see the intuition on all but the most obscure cases. I think my ZBF2L is fairly fast, though still needs lots of improvement, and is probably only about 2 seconds slower than my Fridrich F2L, and on a good ZB average (sub-17) probably only 1 second or less. Moving on from ZBF2L: Ok so I saved ZBLL for last since it is so ridiculously huge. I am learning this by orientation cases with COLL cases as subgroups within an orientation case. I like this way since you can practice the algs by learning the transformation algs from your unknown OLL case into a known OLL case. I think this aids with learning, but is probably not the most optimal way for maximizing your speed while learning. I think optimally you should take your slowest COLL case and learn all the ZBLL algs for it. Then move on to your next slowest, until you know all 40 COLL cases. --------- Side notes: I think OLL, although not necessary for true ZB, should be required for learning ZB. I've found that sometimes I can use a multislotting trick to solve the 3rd and 4th corner edge pair very quickly and save a second or two. In this situation I would much rather do that, then end with OLL and PLL than to solve the 3rd pair only, then hope for a good ZBF2L for the 4th pair, then hope for a ZBLL case that you know. I think when you know 100% ZBLL this might also still be fast, assuming you have a well refined OLL/PLL combo. ---------------- I have no idea if this is the most efficient way, but I like the ability to know just based on orientation whether or not I know a case. For example if I see the T orientation I know immediately that I can do ZBLL. If I see the "L" I know I don't know any algs for it and would just use COLL/PLL. I think having your ZBLL algs spread out over different OLL cases by learning your slowest COLL case would probably be faster in the long run, but would take my skill with recognition when first starting with ZBLL. Also I think COLL/PLL is a bad idea for COLL cases you don't know. It can be fast, and the 1/12 PLL skip is nice, but some of the algs are so horribly slow for COLL. I think maybe using only fast COLL cases would be the best idea. The rest of the time you could just do OLL/PLL. Anyone have any opinions here? ---------------- Let's try to figure out the best way to learn this method. I really don't feel that the number of ZBLL algs is too many, even for recognition. However, in terms of learning them I think there must be better ways to approach it than others. Chris
8. Learning pace for ZBF2L (how to learn it quickly)
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 05:30:24 -0000

More posts here, I'm trying to start as many discussion threads as I can. When I first started learning ZBF2L, my first jump into ZB algs, I felt overwhelmed at first on how to learn them. Pretty quickly though I adopted a technique that worked very well for me, and let me average almost 2.5 algs per day. Within each ZBF2L case there are 8 edge cases (fewer for nicely symmetric F2L cases). Here is how you can approach an F2L case (all 8 subcases) and learn them in three days or less and average 2.5-4 algs per day for learning. Day 1: Look at all 8 algs for your chosen F2L case. Do them over an over again on your cube. Don't just do the alg, but set up with the inverse of the solving alg so each time you see the case the algs solves. Concentrate today only on how to differentiate each case from the other 7. Give them names, or associate them with a picture. Just be able to know how to "see" each case today. Try to setup and solve each alg 20 times or so. Day 2: Again try to do each alg about 20 times by setting it up and then solving it. Today though, focus on memorizing the first 2-3 moves of each alg. You should already comfortably be able to diffentiate them, now just associate with each case the first say 2 moves of the alg to solve it. Remember to do each alg 20 times at least though still. Day 3: Still do each alg 20 times each at least, but now focus on each alg individually and associate with your already memorized first 2-3 moves with the rest of the alg. So once you have done the first 2-3 moves you will be able to recall the rest of the alg. After having done each case at least 60 times already this is easier than it sounds. Now you know all 8 cases fairly solidly within 3 days (sometimes 2). That's a 2.5 algs per day rate. You will be able to recall the algs on a speedsolve but you might delay up to 10-20 seconds or more to recall it. You will, however, retain all 8. After 2-3 weeks you will recognize each case fairly quickly in a speedsolve with minimal delay. After 1 month on average for me, I could recognize all 8 cases within an F2L case extremely smoothly with hardly any delay other than the occasional amnesia. Chris
9. Re: Learning pace for ZBF2L (how to learn it quickly)
From: "Mike Bennett" <mikebennett_one@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 05:40:19 -0000

I like your idea about spreading the learning out over several days, but in practice, I've found I retain algs better if I learn only a few at a time, and practice them until they're second nature. I have a few algs from some COLL cases I've learned, and one ZBF2L case I've learned where I'm getting major amnesia, to the point that I'm going to go back, re-work them out with paper, and memorize the night away as soon as I'm done on this post. They are all from days where I learned several algs and practiced all of them. When I learn an alg, regardless of how many or few others I've learned recently, I always practice it. Generally, about a dozen or so times, just to get the feel of it, and at least two averages worth after that. The next day or so, I do the same. This usually works well for me, but for those few cases where I attempted to learn several at a time, I'm starting to get major amnesia anyhow. Your mileage may vary, though. Maybe I'm just a slow learner. ;) -Mike
10. Learning pace for ZBLL (how to learn it quickly)
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 05:38:05 -0000

It took me 5 months to learn the T orientaton, but I think an entire orientatiton can be learned in 4.5 months as you get further into ZBLL learning. How I do it is this. For each ZBLL case I use ACube to find algs in the metrics I like. I usually search for quarter turn optimal algs in the [RUL] group or [RUF] group first. I have ACube display all algs, not just optimal cases. Then I have ACube search for all algs with all available moves and I have it display all algs found, not just optimal cases. Then I sift through the huge lists of algs to find the good ones (most are easily recognizable as horrible algs for speedcubing). I then get down to 2-3 algs that are very nice. I then use Netcube to time each alg. I don't memorize the algs I just read them off and time my execution of each one. After 20-30 repeitions you can do each of the 2-3 algs without reading off the ACube printout since they are in very short term memory. Play with each alg and find the one that seems to be the fastest. Now that you have chosen an alg, do it 30-40 more times and time each trial with ACube. By this point it is fairly well in your short term memory. Then before you go to bed do the alg a few times again and by then you will have it memorized fairly well and can use it in speedsolves. It usually takes ACube a day to a day and a half to find algs, then I spend either the second half day or full day trying to find the best alg and learn it. So for ZBLL I average about 2 days per alg. For you guys learning from either my or Dan's site I imagine you can learn faster since you can skip the alg searching phase. I've found that often I really dislike the Bernard Helmstetter algs, so I will continue to generate all of mine with ACube. If anyone is interested I can post the results for each case, or at least the algs that I sift through to be the best ones. I don't have the files for most of the T cases, but I do for the last 1 or 2 COLL cases as well as all the U cases I know so far. Let me know if you're interested in this fairly good algs. People have different styles, so I may have weeded out an alg that you would have kept though, so these lists might still not be optimal for your hands. Chris

13. Re: Learning pace for ZBF2L (how to learn it quickly)
From: "Bob Burton" <bob@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 14:33:46 -0000

My approach to learning COLL was similar to your approach of learning ZBF2L, but a little different. I learned COLL in about 13 days, so it was just about 3 algs per day. This is what I did: Day 1: Learn how to perform/finger trick every alg of a given orientation. For example, all 6 of the "T" orientation. Don't worry about what they look like, just keep on performing them over and over so your hands know how to do it. Day 2: Decide how you want to recognize that case and spend the entire day distinguishing between each case and associating each alg to their respective cases. **Note: I learned COLL over the summer. Even though I was working, I had no schoolwork and could devote several hours per day to learn algorithms. ~ Bob --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > > More posts here, I'm trying to start as many discussion threads as I can. > > When I first started learning ZBF2L, my first jump into ZB algs, I > felt overwhelmed at first on how to learn them. 16. learning ZB and practicing your old method
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 17:10:42 -0000

What is the best way to do this? I've found that long periods of practicing only ZB do not make my Fridrich times worse, and often switching back to Fridrich I get averages that, for me, are quite good. My guess is that the number of algs required for Fridrich "seems" fewer than before after being used to ZB recognition and that I make decisions fairly fast, again fast for me, at each step. I've noticed that around tournament time I stop practicing ZB altogether in order to make sure I'm ok for Fridrich, which means 2-4 weeks of no learning for ZB. Is there a way to balance, or is this stop and start the best way to learn ZB and yet still be competitive in competitions? What does everyone think? Any ideas? I seem to be using this stop and start technique. Stop learning ZB before a tournament and start again right afterward. Is there a better way to balance two methods, or not really? Chris
17. Re: learning ZB and practicing your old method
From: "Bob Burton" <bob@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 17:28:01 -0000

Well, of course, since PLL is involved in ZB, it is only the OLL that you would have to worry about forgetting. However, I am sure you have known the OLLs long enough now that you probably won't ever forget them, even if you never practice them again. Since there is less to look for in OLL than ZBLL, your recognition should be fast in comparision. I think start/stop is the best approach. I think my approach will probably be to start ZB and then not stop ZB except for competitions. Even then, though, I think I want to only practice Fridrich at the competition, since I plan on eventually abandoning it (unless I decide ZB will be slower than Fridrich for me). I am looking at the big picture: 2-4 weeks of stopping ZB to practice Fridrich means that it will take me an extra 2-4 weeks to learn ZB. Multiply this time by every competition (and you know I go to a lot of them) and it will add a significant amount of learning time. I am not sure of this yet because I am not in this situation yet, but this is my plan as of now. ~ Bob --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > > What is the best way to do this? I've found that long periods of > practicing only ZB do not make my Fridrich times worse, and often > switching back to Fridrich I get averages that, for me, are quite good. > > My guess is that the number of algs required for Fridrich "seems" > fewer than before after being used to ZB recognition and that I make > decisions fairly fast, again fast for me, at each step. > > I've noticed that around tournament time I stop practicing ZB > altogether in order to make sure I'm ok for Fridrich, which means 2-4 > weeks of no learning for ZB. > > Is there a way to balance, or is this stop and start the best way to > learn ZB and yet still be competitive in competitions? > > What does everyone think? 18. My approach to learning ZB
From: "Jason Baum" <speedrunningcuber@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 18:14:50 -0000

Hi guys, For a while I had been debating on what the best way to learn ZB would be; if it would be better to learn ZBF2L then ZBLL, or learn ZBLL then ZBF2L. I think I've come up with a pretty good way to do both though, and I'm going to try using it from now on. I know about 40 ZBF2L algs so far. Going by Chris' ZBF2L page, I know all of cases 1, 2, 3, 5, and 13 (including reflections). I can convert any case that I don't know into case 1 or 13 very easily, and the ones that aren't easy to convert I know the ZBF2L cases for (excluding case 4, which I'll learn next). So, I can use ZBF2L on every solve without too much extra effort. I feel I can use this to my advantage to start working on ZBLL now. It seems pointless to start ZBLL without knowing any of ZBF2L, but if I can use ZBF2L on every solve even without knowing that many cases, then why not start learning ZBLL? At the same time though, I don't want to completely abandon learning ZBF2L algs. So here's what I've decided to do. For ZBF2L, I'm going to use Chris' technique of spreading each case out over a three day time span and learning them all on the third day. At the same time though, I will try and learn one ZBLL each day. So, for approximately every 8 ZBF2L algs, I will learn 3 ZBLL algs. I think this should be completely managable, and this is nice because by the time I'm done learning ZBF2L, I'll already have a decent chunk of ZBLL down (about 1 1/2 orientation cases). With practice, I think that one ZBLL case per day is very doable, and Chris has already proven that his 3 day ZBF2L method works fine, so why not combine the two? Of course, if this does prove to be too much, I will try a different learning method. However, this sounds like a nice way to focus both on ZBF2L and ZBLL without overloading your brain. Let me know what you guys think! -Jason
19. ZBLL averages
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 10 Nov 2005 20:20:46 -0000

Hey everyone, These are my first ever ZBLL averages. I only know the T, so I had to set it up with a transformation if it wasn't already a T case after ZBF2L. For solves that were already the T orientation after ZBF2L I tried to start from a random angle, and when I needed to do a transformation into T I did the transformation without looking then started the timer when I first saw each case. So basically these averages include the recognition time for ZBLL as well. 05.50, 05.99, 05.35, 05.25, 04.98, 06.58, (03.22), (07.97), 07.12, 06.67, 05.64, 6.56 = 5.96 05.34, 09.58, 04.88, 06.94, 05.50, 05.29, (09.94), 05.11, 06.83, 04.36, 05.05, (03.04) = 5.89 That's actually pretty good for me even if I was doing Fridrich LL. I had some long delays on the case 6 algs for my ZBLL T algs since I recently learned them. I think in 6 months when I know all the T algs second nature that I can easily get sub-5 on average. So I think a sub-5 average is possible for ZBLL algs that you know very well. Maybe after 2-3 years of knowing ZBLL that could even get to low 4.xx, who knows? With all easy cases I think a sub-4 might be possible, though those types of averages would be infrequent. Anyway I thought this was promising, since it shows that even with delays on cases that I recently learned, I can get times that compare to a fairly good Fridrich LL average (for me). I think ZBLL will definitely be managable, even with recognition. Chris

For > you guys learning from either my or Dan's site I imagine you can learn > faster since you can skip the alg searching phase. > > I've found that often I really dislike the Bernard Helmstetter algs, > so I will continue to generate all of mine with ACube. > > If anyone is interested I can post the results for each case, or at > least the algs that I sift through to be the best ones. I don't have > the files for most of the T cases, but I do for the last 1 or 2 COLL > cases as well as all the U cases I know so far. > > Let me know if you're interested in this fairly good algs. People > have different styles, so I may have weeded out an alg that you would > have kept though, so these lists might still not be optimal for your > hands. > > Chris >

26. Re: ACube
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 03:57:09 -0000

Hey Santiago, What I do is this. Open up the command window by clicking on "start", then "run", then type in "command" and click on "OK" If you don't use windows then get to a place where you can run a java program from a command screen. In the windows command program you have to change directories to where your files are for ACube using the tradional DOS directory commands. Once you get to the right directory, type in this java -cp ACube3.jar ACube Now after that line you have a few options for attributes. You can have the program search in either face turn metric, slice turn metric, or quarter turn metric. Your other options are to search for optimal length algs or algs of any length, and also for the program to print out every alg it finds or only a small portion. The commands I use to search for ZBLL algs are these: java -cp ACube3.jar ACube q a The "q" means to search in quartern turn metrics and the "a" means print out every single alg. Once I've analyzed the positions in that metric I exit the program with "Ctrl + C" and start it again with java -cp ACube3.jar ACube a This searches in face turn metric (face turn is the default) and prints out every alg it finds. I then compare the best quarter turn algs and best face turn algs and try to find the best alg among those. If you are comfortable with slice moves, which I am not, then you would also want to use this search string java -cp ACube3.jar ACube s a -------------- Once in ACube you have to decide which types of turns you want to allow, and you have to input the position. While in quarter turn searching (java -cp ACube3.jar ACube q a) I often start with searching for [RUL] only algs. To do this I have to come up with the octet that represents R U and L only. The order of the faces is UDFBLRESM I only want to allow R U and L so I would go through and put a "0" on the face I don't want to allow and a "1" on the one I do want to allow. UDFBLRESM 100011000 Now break this up into three groups of three numbers. 100 011 000 and convert each group of three numbers to decimal. 100 = 4 in decimal. 011 = 3 in decimal. and 000 = 0 in decimal. Now put those numbers together and you get 430 So to search for RUL only moves type "430" then a space then the cube position. I also like to do RULM moves which is 431 by the same process. Now you have to input the cube state. I'll input the T-orientation case ZBLL alg that has all corners in the correct spot and the edges are in the H permutation. So UBR is rotated counter-clockwise, UBL is rotated clockwise, UF and UB switch, and UR and UL switch. In ACube this is: UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! The edges are in the order UF UR UB UL DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL and the corners are in the order UFR UBR UBL UFL DFR DFL DBL DBR The "!!" is short for everything past the last entry is in the correct spot and oriented correctly. A "!" means that single piece is solved and oriented correclty. Typing "!!" only goes through the end of that type of piece. So I have to type it once to say that all the remaining corners are ok, and again at the end to say that all the remaining edges are ok. So UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! is short for UB UL UF UR DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL UFR -UBR +UBL UFL DFR DFL DBL DBR The "-" means that corner is rotated counter-clockwise and the "+" means it is rotated clockwise. A "-" in front of an edge means the edges is flipped. So to search for a RULM moves only solution to the above ZBLL case you would type : 431 UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! Here are some useful face searches that I use a lot: RUL = 430 RULM = 431 URF = 510 URLD = 630 URLF = 530 URFD = 710 Hope that helps some, Chris --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "Santiago" <hiei_jaganshi_333@y...> wrote: > > Hi Chris, i'm new at this, can you tell me how work the ACube?? i > don't know how too use it, and the txt file doesn't help me. Thanks > > Santiago from Argentina > > www.speedcubing.com.ar >
27. COLL/EPLL or OLL/PLL for ZBLL cases you don't know?
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 04:22:25 -0000

Hey everyone, Ever since I started I've been using COLL/EPLL (edge PLL) for ZBLL cases I don't know. I think COLL/PLL is slower than OLL/PLL though, so I've been working on that lately. It's hard to get used to, but I think with time it will be faster. The problem is your chance for 1 look LL changes dramatically between the two. In order for a EPLL skip to count as non-lucky for speedcubing.com you have to have a 20% or greater chance to skip the step you skipped. For COLL/PLL the 1/12 chance to skip EPLL helps tremendously. However if you change that to the odds for OLL or PLL skip then things change. Here are the numbers for how many ZBLL algs you have to know in order to count your skips as non-lucky for COLL/PLL and OLL/PLL COLL/PLL (1/27) + (4/27)*(x/72) + (22/27)*(1/12) = 0.2 x = 46.2 or 47. So you have to know basically 4 COLL cases and use all the PLL and COLL/PLL on any case you don't know. OLL/PLL (1/27) + (4/27)*(x/72) + (22/27)*[(1/27)*(71/72) + (26/27)*(1/72) + (1/27)*(1/72)] = 0.2 x = 59.24 or 60 So you have to know 60 ZBLL algs or 5 full COLL cases in order for OLL/PLL step skip solves to be non-lucky for speedcubing.com The only reason I say this is that you will start to get skip solves a lot that are faster than your pb solves with Fridrich. In order to count those on speedcubing.com though, you have to use the above strategies at the right time. This assumes you know all ZBF2L. At 4 COLL cases use COLL/PLL on *every* ZBLL case you don't know and any skip solve that was previously lucky now counts for speedcubing.com lists. After 5 full COLL cases you can use OLL/PLL on any COLL case you don't know and still have your skip solves count for speedcubing.com Just some ways to stay motivated along the way :-D So benchmark #1 is 4 COLL cases to have non lucky skip step solves. Then benchmark #2 is to get to 5 COLL cases so that you can switch to OLL/PLL which is faster, and still have skip step solves non-lucky. Chris

29. Fixing corner orientation and/or permutaion
From: "Mike Bennett" <mikebennett_one@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 04:55:44 -0000

With the last c/e pair, I often attempt to influence my corner orientation on some of the simpler c/e cases. For example, from Chris' list, the first and some other assorted cases from groups 1, 6, and 13, I would see if any U turns I could perform before or during insertion would grant me a better corner orientation (which comes in mighty useful considering I only know one alg from the Bruno COLL case at present). I was curious what the odds of OLL skips after ZBF2L change to when you only use these cases and what they are like after accounting for trying to fix corners. I'm also curious how difficult it would be to try to always fix corner permutation during the last pair. Certainly, it would add a lot of algs, whether memorized or intuitive, to the ZBF2L plate, but it would drastically reduce the number of necessary ZBLL algs. As someone who is planning to learn all only the ZB algs for correctly permuted corners (and perhaps a few other special cases), this seems very appealing. I'm just looking for someone else's take on the idea, because I don't recall anyone ever mentioning it before. I'm highly interested in learning more about this, if it can prove at all useful and manageable. -Mike
30. Re: Fixing corner orientation and/or permutaion
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 05:14:28 -0000

Hey Mike, (see comments below) > With the last c/e pair, I often attempt to influence my corner > orientation on some of the simpler c/e cases. > > For example, from Chris' list, the first and some other assorted cases > from groups 1, 6, and 13, I would see if any U turns I could perform > before or during insertion would grant me a better corner orientation > (which comes in mighty useful considering I only know one alg from the > Bruno COLL case at present). > > I was curious what the odds of OLL skips after ZBF2L change to when > you only use these cases and what they are like after accounting for > trying to fix corners. I really like trying to work out odds and scenarios. I don't think I fully understand what you are doing yet, but I'd love to try to work out the odds for you. Do you mean that you still do a ZBF2L (flip all LL edges correctly after having solved the last c/e pair) and in addition orient some or all of the corners? Would you make sure that you have say at least 1, or at least 2, or all corners solved? > > I'm also curious how difficult it would be to try to always fix corner > permutation during the last pair. Certainly, it would add a lot of > algs, whether memorized or intuitive, to the ZBF2L plate, but it would > drastically reduce the number of necessary ZBLL algs. As someone who > is planning to learn all only the ZB algs for correctly permuted > corners (and perhaps a few other special cases), this seems very > appealing. What about this, you could learn all the algs to both orient edges and place all corners for ZBF2L case 1 and 13. I imagine for each ZBF2L case there would be around 12 algs not including reflections that you would need to also move corners. So for 16 cases you would need 12 for each of them so that's 192 algs for ZBF2L (a little more than full ZBF2L) but it would reduce your ZBLL count to the ones with just correct corners (84 I believe). That would take fewer algs than ZB, and I imagine it would be pretty fast. For F2L on the last c/e pair you could either pair up the corner and edge or form them into case 13, then use the required alg to flip edge, permute corners, and solve the c/e pair. Then you would have 84 possibilities for the truncated ZBLL solve. I think it would lose a little bit of time off regular ZB by having to either form case 1 or case 13 with the corner and edge (max 5-6 moves I would guess? maybe 7 moves on a very very small number of cases). The recognition for the extended ZBF2L would be a bit longer than regular ZBF2L as well. So the only time you add is maybe an extra second for recognition, plus .75-1.0 seconds for forming the pair. I believe with mastery of ZBF2L that sub-14 is possible for ZB, so with an extra up to 2 seconds you could expect this method to average 15 seconds? Myabe even sub-15 with good cases over the average? I think it shouldn't lose much time off regular ZB, and it requires far fewer cases to learn. I think the method seems sound personally. Chris > > I'm just looking for someone else's take on the idea, because I don't > recall anyone ever mentioning it before. I'm highly interested in > learning more about this, if it can prove at all useful and manageable. > > -Mike >

From: "Santiago" <hiei_jaganshi_333@...>

Ok, Thanks!! i tell you if works! Santiago www.speedcubing.com.ar --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > > Hey Santiago, > > What I do is this. Open up the command window by clicking on "start", > then "run", then type in "command" and click on "OK" > > If you don't use windows then get to a place where you can run a java > program from a command screen. > > In the windows command program you have to change directories to where > your files are for ACube using the tradional DOS directory commands. > > Once you get to the right directory, type in this > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube > > Now after that line you have a few options for attributes. You can > have the program search in either face turn metric, slice turn metric, > or quarter turn metric. Your other options are to search for optimal > length algs or algs of any length, and also for the program to print > out every alg it finds or only a small portion. > > The commands I use to search for ZBLL algs are these: > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube q a > > The "q" means to search in quartern turn metrics and the "a" means > print out every single alg. > > Once I've analyzed the positions in that metric I exit the program > with "Ctrl + C" and start it again with > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube a > > This searches in face turn metric (face turn is the default) and > prints out every alg it finds. > > I then compare the best quarter turn algs and best face turn algs and > try to find the best alg among those. If you are comfortable with > slice moves, which I am not, then you would also want to use this > search string > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube s a > > -------------- > > Once in ACube you have to decide which types of turns you want to > allow, and you have to input the position. > > While in quarter turn searching (java -cp ACube3.jar ACube q a) I > often start with searching for [RUL] only algs. To do this I have to > come up with the octet that represents R U and L only. > > The order of the faces is UDFBLRESM > > I only want to allow R U and L so I would go through and put a "0" on > the face I don't want to allow and a "1" on the one I do want to allow. > > UDFBLRESM > 100011000 > > Now break this up into three groups of three numbers. 100 011 000 and > convert each group of three numbers to decimal. 100 = 4 in decimal. > 011 = 3 in decimal. and 000 = 0 in decimal. > > Now put those numbers together and you get 430 > > So to search for RUL only moves type "430" then a space then the cube > position. I also like to do RULM moves which is 431 by the same process. > > Now you have to input the cube state. I'll input the T-orientation > case ZBLL alg that has all corners in the correct spot and the edges > are in the H permutation. > > So UBR is rotated counter-clockwise, UBL is rotated clockwise, UF and > UB switch, and UR and UL switch. > > In ACube this is: > UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! > > The edges are in the order UF UR UB UL DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL > and the corners are in the order UFR UBR UBL UFL DFR DFL DBL DBR > > The "!!" is short for everything past the last entry is in the correct > spot and oriented correctly. A "!" means that single piece is solved > and oriented correclty. Typing "!!" only goes through the end of that > type of piece. So I have to type it once to say that all the > remaining corners are ok, and again at the end to say that all the > remaining edges are ok. > > So UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! is short for > UB UL UF UR DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL UFR -UBR +UBL UFL DFR DFL DBL DBR > > The "-" means that corner is rotated counter-clockwise and the "+" > means it is rotated clockwise. A "-" in front of an edge means the > edges is flipped. > > So to search for a RULM moves only solution to the above ZBLL case you > would type : > 431 UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! > > Here are some useful face searches that I use a lot: > RUL = 430 > RULM = 431 > URF = 510 > URLD = 630 > URLF = 530 > URFD = 710 > > Hope that helps some, > Chris > > --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "Santiago" <hiei_jaganshi_333@y...> > wrote: > > > > Hi Chris, i'm new at this, can you tell me how work the ACube?? i > > don't know how too use it, and the txt file doesn't help me. Thanks > > > > Santiago from Argentina > > > > www.speedcubing.com.ar > > >

38. Re: [zbmethod] Advantages of ZBF2L
From: Gilles van den Peereboom <gillesvdp@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 23:33:20 +0100

I'm still wondering if the zb method is really worth it. I mean, it's just another way so solve the LL in 2 looks with a more complicated recognition. I think the only way to really improve the Fridrich system is to start learning the LL in one alg. That, as I see it, would be a very interesting improvement. That's why I'm thinking learning the ZB-LL as the first step of the LL in one look. There are not so many cases after all. If you want to learn the ZB-F2L, you could learn some other patterns to solve them in one alg. This is still a possibility and I don't know if I'm really going to learn the complete LL in one look (over 5.000 cases) but I think the ZB-LL is very useful. Well, maybe tomorrow morning when I'll re-read this message I'll see that I'm actually completely tired, but I think this makes sense. What do you think ? I was > thinking that the entire ZB solve would still result in two 'looks', so it > seems as though it would be the same as OLL/PLL except you're doing ZBF2L, > then ZBLL. You would solve the first three pairs, then recognize the ZBF2L > case (OLL), then recognize the ZBLL case (PLL). > > It makes more sense to me to learn as many ZBLL cases as you can so that you > can finish the F2L with basic Fridrich and then solve the last layer in one > look. > > It would be a lot easier to recognize the OLL/PLL then it would for the > ZBF2L/ZBLL case, would it not? > > I'm just wondering what the advantage of ZB would be over Fridrich. 39. Re: Advantages of ZBF2L
From: "Mike Bennett" <mikebennett_one@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 11 Nov 2005 22:56:59 -0000

Look at things this way: ZBF2L really only adds a few moves to most of your solves, and none to several. ZBLL shortens the number of moves for your LL on average. If you could learn full ZB, you should be able to average 45 moves or less. Fridrich takes around 55 on average, I think. That's 10 moves, or 2-4 seconds potentially it could save, assuming you have quick recognition. -Mike Bennett

42. Re: Advantages of ZBF2L
From: "Lars Vandenbergh" <lars.vandenbergh@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 12 Nov 2005 01:06:59 -0000

I can't really see how learning 1-look LL is better then learning full ZB. With a 1-look LL: * the averge number of moves to solve the complete cube is about the same as with full ZB (about 47 moves). * you would have to learn about 8 times the amount of algorihtms (3915 vesus 798). * recognition would be much tougher since with ZB you spread the work more evenly over the last couple of steps. So it seems to me that you're doing much more work to safe exactly the same amount of moves and time. What are others people opinions on this? Going back to Chris' point on ZBF2L/ZBLL "replacing" OLL/PLL but being more complicated: that's true, but: * any recognition task that is or can be mastered to perfection will in the end become instantaneous and just as fast as an easier recognition task. This just requires practice. * Looking at it this way, you sort of skip the 4th pair and immediately start doing ZBF2L which gives you a signifcant advantage in terms of move count. I'm still very convinced that ZB is the best Fridrich extension that people have come up with so far. Any other idea I've heard so far (and I've heard many), either don't give as much advantage lengthwise and just makes your method more complicated, or either give the same advantage as ZB but require much more learning in the end (Gilles' idea being a good example). I understand why people get discouraged by the number of algorithms you have to learn, but think about how ominous Fridrich seemed when you first learned about it (it certainly was for me!). Although ZB has much more cases, you already have so much expierence from learning your current system that you can rely on and that you can use as a leverage for learning ZB. There's only one way to find out if ZB is worth it: try it! Yeah, that's correct. Using COLL, you have a 8/12 chance of getting a 3 edge cycle, 2/12 chance of getting a Z perm, 1/12 chance of a cross perm, and 1/12 chance of a PLL skip. Recognition will slow you down at first, but with some practice I've found COLL to be pretty helpful most of the time. -Jason --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, Chris Hunt <huntca@g...> wrote: > > Good points Lars. 48. Re: Fixing corner orientation and/or permutaion
From: "Mike Bennett" <mikebennett_one@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 13 Nov 2005 01:03:36 -0000

--- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "Mike Bennett" <mikebennett_one@h...> wrote: > > (see comments below) > > As a quick example, set up this on a solved cube: > > R U2 R' U > > Instead of the normal R U'R, I'd do the inverse of the setup. I can > only do this to cases where a single or double U turn fixes them. Oops. That should be R U2 R' U'. Anyway, I'm getting much better at fixing or altering corner orientation with the last F2L pair. Right now, I can really only use it to fix similar cases to the above, and to change cases with four incorrectly oriented corners to cases with fewer (which I know better). I know that there are simple ways to expand upon this, such as the setup RU2R'U'RUR'U'. You can fix it with the inverse, which is very quick. I know there are probably similar ways to speed up other cases, but I haven't tried to find any yet. Using this, I managed an 18.40 average earlier, beating my previous best average by almost 1 second. I don't know if there are more cases it's easy to fix this way, but I'm curious what the odds to skip the OLL step entirely improve to. I'm wondering if anything more than what I'm using already is worthwhile in terms of moves or time saved. I know that without this, the odds are something like 1/27, or ~3.7%. Added to the 1/12 (8.33%)chance for skipping PLL, that's just over 12% chances for a skipped step every solve. I know this improves the odds slightly, but I'd like to know how much. If anyone has any ideas on how to fix corner permutation instead I'd like to hear them, as well. -Mike

Hey everyone, So I know the french guys have been doing team absolut for a while, and competing against eachother and helping eachother has clearly done wonders for their times. Well Bob Burton and I were talking and we think maybe a team [zb] could do the same for us. Here is the proposal. We all invade the sunday contest every sunday, and we use however much zb techniques we know. This is great practice to time yourself with the new techniques. I mean go all out, make mistakes, try new things with the timer still going, etc. I've found that knowing ZBLL and ZBF2L and speedsolving ZBLL and ZBF2L are two entirely different things, so I think starting early on timing would be a good thing. Also, this would be a good chance for us to motivate eachother to learn more. We can share tips afterward, talk through solves on this group etc.. Also having people see our progress on the sunday contest over time may motivate others to try. So remember, if you want to work on your zb, do the sunday contest and at the end of your quote but something [zb] or ZB or whatever to show that is what you used. Bob and I will be doing this for this week's sunday contest and we would love for everyone to join in! Use whatever you know, even if it's no much! This is a chance to try out your new algs! Hope to see you all there, Chris

55. Re: Team [zb]
From: "Doug Lee" <d_funny007@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 13 Nov 2005 21:10:17 -0000

Ya there is a huge difference between knowing it and speedsolving with it. I can definitely attest to that. Just to introduce myself here a bit. I have been using ideas from the ZB method for roughly 2.5 years now. I started speeedsolving about 6 years ago with CLL/ELL and my own F2L system after having spent a lot of time finding CLL and ELL algs (about a year). At that time I didn't know about the speedsolving community and my times where around 90s. Three years ago I finished learning the COLL set (this was before it was called COLL). Around the same time I started learning the ZBLL cases for no corner permutation (1/6 chance of running into this). I am a relatively slow solver, averaging 22.30 (a non-RA I did last week). I am learning the ZBLL by Corner Permutation category (and CLL sub-categories). I get a 1-look LL about 45% of the time now. Off Chris's ZBF2L page, I know cases 1,2,3,5,13 and a bit of 4,6,7. The reason I get so many 1-look LL is because I know multiple CLL's for each CLL case. Also I do some more advanced stuff during F2L, such as flipping edges on 3rd c/e pair; choosing which of the last two to do as my 3rd pair; and knowing a set of algorithms for partial cross solving. That is availible here: http://www-personal.umich.edu/~dlli/NewAlgSet.html after RichardP requested it. I am working on multiple things now. Learning ZBF2L cases 4,6,7; geting better at regonizing ZBLL cases in the Sune category; and mastering the alg set given above (I have a couple more to go). -Doug --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > I've found that knowing ZBLL and ZBF2L and speedsolving ZBLL and ZBF2L > are two entirely different things, so I think starting early on timing > would be a good thing.

59. First sub 20 average using VH!
From: "Jason Baum" <speedrunningcuber@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sun, 13 Nov 2005 23:09:36 -0000

Hi guys, I just got my first sub 20 using the VH system! 22.65, 18.56, 18.89, 17.36, (25.37), 17.46, 22.28, 20.22, 19.22, 20.76, (17.00), 22.41 ==> 19.98 The 17.46 was a PLL skip using COLL, and on the 18.89 I used ZBLL (took a while to recall it though!). For all of these solves I had to convert the fourth pair into either a pair and instert case or just an insert case. I was really not expecting this because previously my best average with this method was 22.xx. To top it off, this was for the Sunday Contest! On a side note, how many ZB algs do I have to know until I can say I use ZB and not VH? I'm feeling very good about this method right now. I think that once I know more of it, I'll be getting some very nice times! :P -Jason team [zb]

61. Re: Definition of VH system.
From: "Jason Baum" <speedrunningcuber@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 14 Nov 2005 00:07:19 -0000

Hi Chris, You have it right except for the 4th pair. VHF2L is done in two steps. First, you pair up the fourth pair. Then, you insert it while orienting LL edges. I'm not sure if the pair+insert cases count as VHF2L or ZBF2L, though. But yeah, VH is basically just a simplified form of the ZB method. -Jason --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, Chris Hunt <huntca@g...> wrote: > > Although not ZB, I thought this might be related because it is my belief > that both these systems orient the edges of the LL while simultaneously > placing the final pair. > > I looked somewhere for a formal definition of the VH system and couldn't > find it! Please let me know if I understand the VH system correctly: > > 1) Cross > 2) 3 F2L pairs > 3) 4th pair, while orienting LL edges at the same time > 4) Finish with COLL and EPLL, or just PLL if the corners are already > oriented correctly. > > Is this correct? If so, I guess it makes sense to learn VH and then move to > ZB. > > -Chris >

71. Re: Team [zb]
From: "Doug Lee" <d_funny007@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Mon, 14 Nov 2005 03:14:24 -0000

Old habit, I always called it the Bruno. In it's pure form it is the "4 corners" (4 courners twisted but not the "double-superman"), no CP and a specific 3 edge cycle. To me Bruno=R' U2 R2 U R2 U R2 U2 R'. It goes by the names in team BLD as "The Wheel", "Four Corners" and "Pie". I think these 4 terms are pretty standard now. It can be extended to include all the ones in that COLL case (those w/o CP). Or it can be extended to what DanH, Hardwick (I think), and I call the Pi-Orientation. It's all the ZBLL cases with all 4 corners twisted (the less symmetric of the two). It really depends on the context. However I'd prefer it to be stated clearly as there seems to be confusion frequently. -Doug --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, Brent Morgan <brentmorganmaster@y...> wrote: > > Good question... What are these 'Bruno' coll cases... > > -Brent Morgan > Team [ZB] > > Chris Hunt <huntca@g...> wrote: > I think this might be the fourth time I've seen you say 'Bruno'. 75. Intuitive vs. Concrete
From: "Mike Bennett" <mikebennett_one@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 15 Nov 2005 03:09:19 -0000

I've been doing a lot of thinking, now that I've learned all of my COLL and have begun tackling ZBF2L in earnest, and a lot of it has centered on whether it's better to use an intuitive or rigid approach to ZBF2L. Both have their benefits: Rigid approach probably affords faster recognition and execution. This can lead to great times. Chris Hardwick is a testament to this. Intuitive approach makes for less to learn, helps you understand the way the cube works more so you get less amnesia, and allows you to optimize on the fly. I think throughout ZBF2L, I'm going to try to learn as many algorithms intuitively as possible, because I like the benefits more. I can perform many of them from more than one angle, and I can often fix or influence corner orientation along the way. Is anyone else attempting to learn algs like this, or does everyone try to learn the cases, rather than what's going on with the cube? -Mike P.S. Where has our fearless leader been? Some of us are eagerly awaiting replies. ;)

77. Re: Intuitive vs. Concrete
From: "Doug Lee" <d_funny007@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 15 Nov 2005 04:30:55 -0000

I memorize the ZBF2L cases intuitively. There really aren't that many algs in my arsenal that I don't understand and apply blindly. I'd like to keep it that way. When learning a ZBF2L alg, I'll disect it into parts: if it's a conjugator, if it messes with a cross edge, if it transforms it into another ZBF2L case... etc. I also know all the secondary effects of my COLL algs. So I pick between doing it or it's mirror depending on edges. -Doug --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, Chris Hunt <huntca@g...> wrote: > > As I am still in the process of learning COLL, I am currently doing ZBF2L > intuitively as well. 85. One more reason I like ZB so much
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Tue, 15 Nov 2005 16:40:10 -0000

Hey everyone, I'm really going to being in earnest with this "one parity" method for the 4x4x4. Bascailly it entails using the COLL case to identify whether or not your have double parity or just single parity whenever you see the OLL parity. I'm going to complete all the orientation pages and COLL images on my ZBLL page in order to use it as a study aid. I will continue to only add the actual algorithms as I learn them. I really only post an alg once I know it through and through, so that won't change. If you're interested in this method, let me know and I can explain more about it. ZB is what gave me the idea to try it, and since working out better solutions to the parity algs is the hot topic for 4x4x4 solving right now I want to pursue it pretty hard myself. So ZB helps for other cubes, not just the 3x3x3. The advantage to using the "one-parity" method is also that ZBLL becomes a viable option on 4x4x4 since you can be certain of a true ZBLL case without parity. Something to think about if you're interested in using your new ZB stuff to help for the larger cubes as well. Chris team [zb]

Open up the command window by clicking on "start", > then "run", then type in "command" and click on "OK" > > If you don't use windows then get to a place where you can run a java > program from a command screen. > > In the windows command program you have to change directories to where > your files are for ACube using the tradional DOS directory commands. > > Once you get to the right directory, type in this > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube > > Now after that line you have a few options for attributes. You can > have the program search in either face turn metric, slice turn metric, > or quarter turn metric. Your other options are to search for optimal > length algs or algs of any length, and also for the program to print > out every alg it finds or only a small portion. > > The commands I use to search for ZBLL algs are these: > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube q a > > The "q" means to search in quartern turn metrics and the "a" means > print out every single alg. > > Once I've analyzed the positions in that metric I exit the program > with "Ctrl + C" and start it again with > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube a > > This searches in face turn metric (face turn is the default) and > prints out every alg it finds. > > I then compare the best quarter turn algs and best face turn algs and > try to find the best alg among those. If you are comfortable with > slice moves, which I am not, then you would also want to use this > search string > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube s a > > -------------- > > Once in ACube you have to decide which types of turns you want to > allow, and you have to input the position. > > While in quarter turn searching (java -cp ACube3.jar ACube q a) I > often start with searching for [RUL] only algs. To do this I have to > come up with the octet that represents R U and L only. > > The order of the faces is UDFBLRESM > > I only want to allow R U and L so I would go through and put a "0" on > the face I don't want to allow and a "1" on the one I do want to allow. > > UDFBLRESM > 100011000 > > Now break this up into three groups of three numbers. 100 011 000 and > convert each group of three numbers to decimal. 100 = 4 in decimal. > 011 = 3 in decimal. and 000 = 0 in decimal. > > Now put those numbers together and you get 430 > > So to search for RUL only moves type "430" then a space then the cube > position. I also like to do RULM moves which is 431 by the same process. > > Now you have to input the cube state. I'll input the T-orientation > case ZBLL alg that has all corners in the correct spot and the edges > are in the H permutation. > > So UBR is rotated counter-clockwise, UBL is rotated clockwise, UF and > UB switch, and UR and UL switch. > > In ACube this is: > UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! > > The edges are in the order UF UR UB UL DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL > and the corners are in the order UFR UBR UBL UFL DFR DFL DBL DBR > > The "!!" is short for everything past the last entry is in the correct > spot and oriented correctly. A "!" means that single piece is solved > and oriented correclty. Typing "!!" only goes through the end of that > type of piece. So I have to type it once to say that all the > remaining corners are ok, and again at the end to say that all the > remaining edges are ok. > > So UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! is short for > UB UL UF UR DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL UFR -UBR +UBL UFL DFR DFL DBL DBR > > The "-" means that corner is rotated counter-clockwise and the "+" > means it is rotated clockwise. A "-" in front of an edge means the > edges is flipped. > > So to search for a RULM moves only solution to the above ZBLL case you > would type : > 431 UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! > > Here are some useful face searches that I use a lot: > RUL = 430 > RULM = 431 > URF = 510 > URLD = 630 > URLF = 530 > URFD = 710 > > Hope that helps some, > Chris > > --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "Santiago" hiei_jaganshi_333@y... > wrote: > > > > Hi Chris, i'm new at this, can you tell me how work the ACube?? i > > don't know how too use it, and the txt file doesn't help me. Thanks > > > > Santiago from Argentina > > > > www.speedcubing.com.ar > > >

96. Messing around with transformation solving
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 02:03:54 -0000

Hey everyone, I just did an average using transformations sometimes instead of always COLL when I don't know the ZBLL algs for the COLL case. Basically, on my slowest COLL cases I do the transformation into T instead of COLL, since the transformations are all suney type algs and the T is a ZBLL alg. 17.24, 17.52, 17.46, (14.44), 21.18, (30.01), 16.94, 19.01, 18.94, 22.21, 18.55, 16.20 = 18.52 The 16.94 was actually transforming either an S or AS orientation into T then doing the T alg. Some solves were straight ZB, some were fast COLL. The 16.20 at the very end was a straight ZB solve, I knew the ZBLL case, and I think 1 of the 17's also. I kind of like this, since some of my COLL cases are horrible, and I think it might be faster to do the transformation then a T alg. I'm going to mess around with this some more, but even with only beginning to do this I can get sub-19 with it. I think this method will definitely be worth considering for when you know a full orientation case. I don't mean to brag here, I'm not trying to rub in knowing the T orientation. I just know that you guys will all be to this point very shortly, so I'm trying to mess around with new techniques and hopefully you guys will know a really good strategy for handling your non-ZBLL case solves better than COLL/PLL by the time you get her. I definitely agree with Mike that COLL/EPLL is not a good LL strategy in the long run, so I'm trying to find new things as well. Mike I do remember those posts on the regular speedsolving group a while back, and though I disagreed then I have come to agree now with more practice. Chris

98. Re: Messing around with transformation solving
From: "cmhardw" <foozman17@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 04:11:54 -0000

Hey Matt, I guess I should have clarified a little more ;-) COLL/EPLL is extremely fast, and I think when you factor in the 1/12 chance to skip EPLL that it might be faster than most people's OLL/PLL combos. I think a really good OLL/PLL set of algs though would probably win out. What I don't like is getting a slow COLL case, and ending with a Z permutation. As weird as that sounds, and as much as I like the Z perm in my solving, it is my slowest and longest EPLL alg. That double combination can mean a slow LL time compared to the average COLL/PLL gives you. On this page: http://www.speedcubing.com/chris/zbstats.html I have twice done a 100 cube average that shows the number of moves used in COLL/PLL finish. I get that, including the EPLL skips, COLL/PLL averages 21.12 moves on average. I think Fridrich averages around 19-20 as well so they are fairly close. The problem though, for me, is that keeping the edges oriented for some CLL cases means a slow alg. Having said that though I have managed sub-17 averages using COLL/PLL on ZBLL cases that I don't know. I am certain I have had a full 12 cube sub-17 average that only had EPLL skips for the ZBLL stuff, meaning that sub-17 is definitely possible. I don't think a transformation+ZBLL combo used exclusively would be faster, but rather a combination of COLL/PLL finish (only on fast COLL cases) and transformation+ZBLL on slow COLL cases would be best. I think all of COLL should be required before learning any ZBLL though, since the recognition of ZBLL for me is so heavily based on COLL. I use the block recognition technique for ZBLL, and often the only thing different between three different ZBLL cases is the COLL case. They can have the same block structure, but be different COLL cases. So I would definitely say to learn COLL, and use COLL/EPLL until you finish your first orientation case for ZBLL. After that point, replace your slowest COLL cases with transformations into your ZBLL orientation. At least that is the experiment I am trying, but I have a feeling it has potential to e very fast. So when I say slower, I only mean sometimes. COLL/EPLL is still fast, but I don't think it is the best option. It is, however, still a good one. Chris --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "mgwallisa" <mattwallisa@m...> wrote: > > --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > I > > definitely agree with Mike that COLL/EPLL is not a good LL > strategy in > > the long run, so I'm trying to find new things as well. Mike I do > > remember those posts on the regular speedsolving group a while > back, > > and though I disagreed then I have come to agree now with more > practice. > > > > Chris > >

102. Re: Messing around with transformation solving
From: "Doug Lee" <d_funny007@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 04:44:34 -0000

I'd recommend learning COLL first. At least you can use it in every ZBF2L solve. And you can OLL in cases where you don't ZBF2L it. Learning specific groups of ZBLL means that you don't get to see it much, thus you hardly ever use it (unless you transform to it like Chris does). This means that it would be harder to retain. It's easier to retain algs that you use more frequently. If you learn COLL first, I think you'll start to understand the types of recognition tricks involved for ZBLL (if that is your final goal). -Doug --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "mgwallisa" <mattwallisa@m...> wrote: > > --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > I > > definitely agree with Mike that COLL/EPLL is not a good LL > strategy in > > the long run, so I'm trying to find new things as well. I have been transforming cases as well. When I get to the LL I will flip edges if I haven't already. Then I solve the corner permutation using one of two pre-picked COLLs. (The fastest ones I know for adj swap and diag swap, resp.) If it is a PLL, I'll solve it straight up since I still need work on my PLL. (I only recently mastered... ok maybe not mastered, PLL. Like only a bit over a year.) Else, I do a single Sune (also in pre-picked grippings) to get it into the S-Orientation if it is not already. This way I get to practice my S-Orientation cases (those w/o CP). I pre-pick all my grippings to ensure uniform randomness. -Doug Li --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > > Hey Matt, > > I guess I should have clarified a little more ;-) > > COLL/EPLL is extremely fast, and I think when you factor in the 1/12 > chance to skip EPLL that it might be faster than most people's OLL/PLL > combos. 105. Re: Messing around with transformation solving
From: "Mike Bennett" <mikebennett_one@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 06:28:47 -0000

--- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "cmhardw" <foozman17@h...> wrote: > I kind of like this, since some of my COLL cases are horrible, and I > think it might be faster to do the transformation then a T alg. I'm toying with two possible other routes for solvers, instead of normal ZB. As I see it, when you're finishing your last pair, there are four possible LL substeps you can accomplish with it. Orient edges, as in ZB Orient corners Permute corners Permute edges. I don't think permuting edges would be very effective, because you would be left with edge OLL and COLL without disturbing edges. This leaves the middle two strategies unexamined. The latter of which would leave an interesting combination. Assuming you used ZB cases (however many up to you, but at least 1 and 13)to flip edges first, it would basically leave you with an easy ZB case for the remaining step. It would be an interesting alternative to ZB, but without quite so much potential. Perhaps as an alternative to someone who doesn't want to learn full ZB, but wouldn't mind a reduced number of cases. The former choice seems more interesting to me. There are two possible ways to pursue this option. The first involves learning cases to orient corners only, seeing as this has the greatest number of possible cases concerning these four substeps, it offers the greatest possible rewards for lessening the number of cases for your last step. If you could orient corners with your last pair, simply using cases 1 and 13 that gives us 27*2*2 cases, accounting for symmetry. That gives us 108 cases to learn, compared to the 306 for ZBF2L. Also this leaves us with an intruiging last layer. Essentially, it would give you of the 21 PLL cases, with one of 7 possible edge orientations. As far as recognition is concerned, I think it could be quite fast. The trick would be finding algs that did it quickly. I'm terrible at finding move counts and whatnot, so I don't know if this would prove to even be an improvement over normal CFOP, but I suspect it would be, if only for the reduced number of moves for corner orientation. Alternately, if one were to perform a ZB case 1 or 13 alg *followed* by a corner orienter, this brings your OLL skip percentage to 100%, leaving you with a simple PLL for your LL (except in cases where your fourth pair is finished after you place your third). Again, I'm no expert on move counts, but I would assume exploiting an open slot would be useful. Especially in cases where you've got an easy edge orientaion, this could be quite fast. In fact, I got a 14.25 today with it. Technically I had one pair come up ready to insert and a very easy two move cross, but it was still way faster any of my other solves. Again, I doubt this will approach full ZB in terms of potential, but for those wary of learning several hundred algorithms, this might be a good way to go. Really, it's got 140 F2L cases and 21 LL cases. Anyway, this was all inspired by my foolings with ZB, and may be an interesting path to try. If anyone wants to work out possible move numbers or percentages and things for me, or explain how, that would be fantastic. > I don't mean to brag here, I'm not trying to rub in knowing the T > orientation. I just know that you guys will all be to this point very > shortly, so I'm trying to mess around with new techniques and > hopefully you guys will know a really good strategy for handling your > non-ZBLL case solves better than COLL/PLL by the time you get her. If you have 1/12 odds of a PLL skip with COLL, and the T cases account for about 1/5 of what comes up, that means you have a 1/4 or better chance to come up with a 1 Look LL after learning only this case. I think taking stock of your inventory of COLL algs every now and then to see which cases are slow and which are fast is a good idea anyway. However, if you've already learned all of the T's, now is the time to do it again. Decide based on the orientation case whether or not you're going to do COLL or just transform to the T case. In general, I think you'd want to stick with COLL, simply because recognizing the case to transform into the T and then a ZB alg on top of that would add incredible odds for delay. >I definitely agree with Mike that COLL/EPLL is not a good LL strategy in > the long run, so I'm trying to find new things as well. Mike I do > remember those posts on the regular speedsolving group a while back, > and though I disagreed then I have come to agree now with more practice. Actually, I think I said C/COLL+E/PLL was a bad idea. Too ambiguous and not beneficial enough. It's why I decided to go with straight COLL+PLL. And, at least for me, this is proving far more promising than OLL+PLL. Since I've started learning them a few months ago, I've dropped my best average of 100 down to 19.96. Then again, I think I'll have more luck in the end with COLL+PLL/specialized ZB, but your mileage may vary. > > Chris > Mike team [zb]

There are two ways to divide this further, now that I think about it: permuting after pairing/edge flipping and permuting while pairing/edge flipping. 109. Another idea for solving the cube!
From: "Dan" <dan_j_harris@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Thu, 17 Nov 2005 09:45:30 -0000

HI everyone, Thanks to Chris for pointing out this group to me, I didn't even realise it existed before this morning! :-S Sorry. The ZBLL is dependent on all 4 LL edges being correctly oriented once you finish the F2L. As you get further on in your solution, edge control gets harder and harder, simply because you have less freedom. Recently I have been experimenting with Orienting edges right at the beginning of the solve. Orienting edges and then solving the cross is easy enough to do, but I think you would only reap any benefit from this if you could orient edges AND solve the cross SIMULTANEOUSLY. I suggested to Chris that with a lot of practice, this might be in the same league as solving the XCross, which Chris himself admits he can regularly see now given the 15 seconds inspection. I must note that this idea was not fundamentally mine, it was discussing this possibility with Ron at WC2005 and also hearing about it sometime in the past that caused me to try and work at it. Really, it's the first time I heard about it and had enough cubing experience to know exactly what it means for the rest of the solve ;) Of course, most of you guys are a lot sharper than me, and you would probably realise even now, that if you could have 12correctly oriented edges after the cross is solved, you have 2 advantages. Firstly, you can blaze through the F2L, the number of cases is halved? (intuition tells me this but like most things where intuition is involved ive probably missed a simple counter-example...). But you can speed through it using only R U and L (and D of course, for empty slots), and of course F2 and B2 if necessary. You can even use F and B if it's easier, as long as the algorithm is 2-generator and you replace the cross edge after solving the pair it won't affect the edges! Secondly, once you've solved the F2L, without any work at all (and ensuring you haven't changed edge orientation during F2L), you end up with a ZBLL case by default. I realise a lot of people in this group are learning ZBF2L, and this would render those 300 or so algs redundant. I don't want to "urinate on your bonfire" by any means, I still think it is worth learning since my original idea of orienting edges is still unproved to work, but this is why I am posting about it! But you have to work far less hard to orient edges during the F2L, so you could go at it absolutely full speed, and with the ease of the algorithms perhaps even solve it in 5-6 seconds. However I would like you to consider this idea. So you would proceed: Orient edges + Solve Cross together F2L ZBLL I am currently learning the ZBLL element which is common to both this idea and the full ZB system, so I am not in too far that I can't get out yet ;) I would appreciate some feedback :) DanH :)

Hi everyone, I would appreciate a review of the following algs to see if anybody has any better ones :) Also comments on useful memory/finger tricks for these cases. Dan :) L - BR LB O/A = R U2 R U R2 U R' U' R U R' U2 R' U R' O/C = R U' R U2 R U' R' U R U' R2 U' R' U2 R' O/O = R U2 R' U' R U R' U' R U R' U' R U' R' A/C = R U R2 U' R' U2 R U2 R' U2 R' U R' U2 R A/A left = R' U2 R U' R U2 R U2 R' U2 R U R2 U' R' A/A right = U R2 U R' U' R2 U' R U R U2 R U' R U' R2 A/O = U R2 U R' U' R' U R U R' U R U' R U' R2 (16,18) C/A = R2 U R' U R' U2 R' U' R' U R2 U R U' R2 C/O = R2 U R' U R' U' R U' R' U' R U R U' R2 (16,18) C/C = R U2 R' U2 R' U' R U' R' U2 R U2 R U R' (16,20) OPPX = R' U2 R2 U R' U' R2 U R U' R' U R2 U R2 U' R' (17,22) ADJX = R2 U2 R U' R U R' U2 R U2 R' U R' U' R U2 R (17,22) Dan :)
119. Re: Some L algorithms
From: "Doug Lee" <d_funny007@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Fri, 18 Nov 2005 19:22:03 -0000

I don't understand the naming you choose. I am assuming all these cases are for the no CP cases. I like your first two. It's actually the only ones in this group I have yet to learn. I would have done something horrible like (R'B2)(L2U2'F)(UF'U)(L'B)^2 (R). I'll have to adapt yours. I haven't gone through each and every one of these, but I do use some different algs: Like > OPPX = R' U2 R2 U R' U' R2 U R U' R' U R2 U R2 U' R' I do zU'(R'UR'U')(R2U)z'(R'U2)(RUR'U)R. As for determining which case, I have to pre-adjust the U layer first so that the corners are in place. Then I check for no EP (I have a very fast alg for that); the H-EP (I do a triple sune here); one of the Z-EPs (the one above is the default CLL I have been using for ages, it is a Sune/Sune combination) I will do the analogous Antisune/Antisune combination in the other Z case. What's left are the 3-cycle cases. I sort of do the following: hold it so that I see both LL face colors on the side (holding it on a diagonal), then I look at the edge that needs to go opposite where it is now. If it needs to come towards me I think "in", if it needs to go away I think "out". Next I make note of how many of those two edges in front are out of place. So I would call them "in1","in2","out1", "out2". The nice thing about this way of thinking about it is that the "in's" are the same alg but inverse and so are the "out's". I use a Sune/Sune combination for my "out1" case, and an Antisune/Antisune combination for my "out2" case. I started incorporating this into my solves right after WC. The "in" cases I have yet to learn, seeing as I have a terrible alg for it. The non-3cycle ones I have been actively using since b4 Toronto, so I have mastered those. I am curious aobut your naming scheme here. -Doug > L - BR > LB > > O/A = R U2 R U R2 U R' U' R U R' U2 R' U R' > O/C = R U' R U2 R U' R' U R U' R2 U' R' U2 R' > O/O = R U2 R' U' R U R' U' R U R' U' R U' R' > > A/C = R U R2 U' R' U2 R U2 R' U2 R' U R' U2 R > A/A left = R' U2 R U' R U2 R U2 R' U2 R U R2 U' R' > A/A right = U R2 U R' U' R2 U' R U R U2 R U' R U' R2 > A/O = U R2 U R' U' R' U R U R' U R U' R U' R2 (16,18) > > C/A = R2 U R' U R' U2 R' U' R' U R2 U R U' R2 > C/O = R2 U R' U R' U' R U' R' U' R U R U' R2 (16,18) > C/C = R U2 R' U2 R' U' R U' R' U2 R U2 R U R' (16,20) > > OPPX = R' U2 R2 U R' U' R2 U R U' R' U R2 U R2 U' R' (17,22) > ADJX = R2 U2 R U' R U R' U2 R U2 R' U R' U' R U2 R (17,22) > > Dan :) >

If you are comfortable with > > > slice moves, which I am not, then you would also want to use this > > > search string > > > > > > java -cp ACube3.jar ACube s a > > > > > > -------------- > > > > > > Once in ACube you have to decide which types of turns you want to > > > allow, and you have to input the position. > > > > > > While in quarter turn searching (java -cp ACube3.jar ACube q a) I > > > often start with searching for [RUL] only algs. To do this I > have to > > > come up with the octet that represents R U and L only. > > > > > > The order of the faces is UDFBLRESM > > > > > > I only want to allow R U and L so I would go through and put > a "0" on > > > the face I don't want to allow and a "1" on the one I do want to > allow. > > > > > > UDFBLRESM > > > 100011000 > > > > > > Now break this up into three groups of three numbers. 100 011 > 000 and > > > convert each group of three numbers to decimal. 100 = 4 in > decimal. > > > 011 = 3 in decimal. and 000 = 0 in decimal. > > > > > > Now put those numbers together and you get 430 > > > > > > So to search for RUL only moves type "430" then a space then the > cube > > > position. I also like to do RULM moves which is 431 by the same > process. > > > > > > Now you have to input the cube state. I'll input the T- > orientation > > > case ZBLL alg that has all corners in the correct spot and the > edges > > > are in the H permutation. > > > > > > So UBR is rotated counter-clockwise, UBL is rotated clockwise, > UF and > > > UB switch, and UR and UL switch. > > > > > > In ACube this is: > > > UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! > > > > > > The edges are in the order UF UR UB UL DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL > > > and the corners are in the order UFR UBR UBL UFL DFR DFL DBL DBR > > > > > > The "!!" is short for everything past the last entry is in the > correct > > > spot and oriented correctly. A "!" means that single piece is > solved > > > and oriented correclty. Typing "!!" only goes through the end of > that > > > type of piece. So I have to type it once to say that all the > > > remaining corners are ok, and again at the end to say that all > the > > > remaining edges are ok. > > > > > > So UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! is short for > > > UB UL UF UR DF DR DB DL FR FL BR BL UFR -UBR +UBL UFL DFR DFL > DBL DBR > > > > > > The "-" means that corner is rotated counter-clockwise and > the "+" > > > means it is rotated clockwise. A "-" in front of an edge means > the > > > edges is flipped. > > > > > > So to search for a RULM moves only solution to the above ZBLL > case you > > > would type : > > > 431 UB UL UF UR !! ! -UBR +UBL !! > > > > > > Here are some useful face searches that I use a lot: > > > RUL = 430 > > > RULM = 431 > > > URF = 510 > > > URLD = 630 > > > URLF = 530 > > > URFD = 710 > > > > > > Hope that helps some, > > > Chris > > > > > > --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "Santiago" > hiei_jaganshi_333@y... > > > wrote: > > > > > > > > Hi Chris, i'm new at this, can you tell me how work the > ACube?? i > > > > don't know how too use it, and the txt file doesn't help me. > Thanks > > > > > > > > Santiago from Argentina > > > > > > > > www.speedcubing.com.ar > > > > > > > > > >

123. Re: Some L algorithms
From: "Dan" <dan_j_harris@...>
To: zbmethod@yahoogroups.com
Date: Sat, 19 Nov 2005 00:06:24 -0000

Hi, Yes sorry, I didnt think that people would pay much attention to the names. The scheme is very simple, to determine the case you look at the coll case which you have (and I use Ron's scheme to determine the coll) Then you need to identify the 12 sub-cases using the edges. x/y means you would look at FU and FUR stickers/RUF and RU stickers, and compare them to one another. C means the colours match, O means opposite, and A means adajcent. There is a more detailed description on my ZB pages where the algs for the T orient are. This is nice because it breaks every step down into recognising a pattern. I'm not sure exactly what I am going to do for the cases where there are 4 twisted corners... but we'll cross that bridge when we come to it :) Perhaps all we need to do is look at a different sticker. Sorry this post is pretty vague, but it's late and I want to go to bed, getting up early to fly to Hungary tomorrow! Dan :) - team[zb] :D --- In zbmethod@yahoogroups.com, "Doug Lee" <d_funny007@y...> wrote: > > I don't understand the naming you choose. (zR2) U' (= R'UR'U') (RUR'U')^2 (x'l'R'U) So the mirror but with cross on left and the= post-adjust in front. From: "Doug Lee" <d_funny007@...>
